\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Bound\_Type}{Bound\_Type}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a77bc362495cfca4cb5d3e1a086a151c5}{omega\+::\+Bound\+\_\+\+Type}}}



Type of conjunct \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_conjunct}{Conjunct}} can be exact or lower or upper bound. 


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item For lower bound conjunct, the upper bound is assumed to be true;
\item For upper bound conjunct, the lower bound is assumed to be false

\index{omega@{omega}!Var\_Kind@{Var\_Kind}}
\index{Var\_Kind@{Var\_Kind}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Var\_Kind}{Var\_Kind}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_ac7ab7017276f7049991d3f73fbbdc1e9}{omega\+::\+Var\+\_\+\+Kind}}}



Variable declaration. 


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Variables are free or quantified.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Free variables are classified as input, output and global.
\item Quantified variables are classified as forall, exists and wildcard.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\item All global variables are functions symbols of (possibly 0) arguments
\item Local variables that correspond to $>$0-\/ary functions are identified as functions of a prefix of the input, output, or both tuples 
\end{DoxyItemize}\begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{Input\_Var@{Input\_Var}!omega@{omega}}\index{omega@{omega}!Input\_Var@{Input\_Var}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceomega_ac7ab7017276f7049991d3f73fbbdc1e9a3c16418ccea8b423efbfff30326c4835}\label{namespaceomega_ac7ab7017276f7049991d3f73fbbdc1e9a3c16418ccea8b423efbfff30326c4835}}

\index{omega@{omega}!AffineHull@{AffineHull}}
\index{AffineHull@{AffineHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{AffineHull()}{AffineHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Affine\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Affine Hull using affine combination. 

Tightest set of equality constraints who\textquotesingle{}s intersection contains all of S.

Affine combination is the convex combination without the positivity constraint a\+\_\+i\+: \[x \in Affine(S) \iff \exists y_i in S, \exists a_i \in R, \sum_i a_i = 1: x = \sum_i a_iy_i\] This will first call approximate on R to eliminate any wildcards and strides \begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a1c21a38b01729e780825f69d73ef7fb9}{Convex\+Hull}}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{ConicHull@{ConicHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ConicHull()}{ConicHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Conic\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Conic Hull using conic combination. 

Conic hull is the tightest cone that contains \mbox{\hyperlink{isl__union__macro_8h_a29bb33138384ad57b7bd137d4b3a432c}{S(\+R)}}.

Conic combination is the convex combination without the unit constraint on a\+\_\+i\+: \[x \in Conic(R) \iff \exists y_i \in R, a_i \geq 0: x = \sum_i a_iy_i\] This will first call approximate on R to eliminate any wildcards and strides \begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a1c21a38b01729e780825f69d73ef7fb9}{Convex\+Hull}}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
Expensive \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceomega_a93996770b836af6364c564ccd2e42ea0}\label{namespaceomega_a93996770b836af6364c564ccd2e42ea0}}

\index{ConvexHull@{ConvexHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ConvexHull()}{ConvexHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Convex\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Convex Hull of R using the convex combination. 

Tightest inequality constraints who\textquotesingle{}s intersection contains all of S. \[x \in Convex(S) \iff \exists y_i \in S, a_i \geq 0, \sum_i a_i = 1: x = \sum_i a_iy_i\]

This will first call approximate on R to eliminate any wildcards and strides.

\index{omega@{omega}!DecoupledConvexHull@{DecoupledConvexHull}}
\index{DecoupledConvexHull@{DecoupledConvexHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DecoupledConvexHull()}{DecoupledConvexHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Decoupled\+Convex\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Decoupled\+Convex Hull of R. 

Decoupled\+Convex\+Hull is the same as Convex\+Hull, except that it only finds constraints that involve both variables x\&y if there is a constraint that involves both x\&y in one of the conjuncts of R. Always contains the convex hull.

This will first call approximate on R to eliminate any wildcards and strides \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceomega_aa7a72550a03b4bd5a55e738286b849cb}\label{namespaceomega_aa7a72550a03b4bd5a55e738286b849cb}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{find\_floor\_definition()}{find\_floor\_definition()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily std\+::pair$<$ bool, \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_g_e_q___handle}{G\+E\+Q\+\_\+\+Handle}} $>$ omega\+::find\+\_\+floor\+\_\+definition (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{gen-psqr_8c_a2c212835823e3c54a8ab6d95c652660e}{const}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a3d38f72333aae2d1dd9b772059c2ee3e}{Variable\+\_\+\+ID}}}]{v,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{gmp__compat_8h_a1e8c092646181d922b1412a0b41dcfde}{std\+::set}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a3d38f72333aae2d1dd9b772059c2ee3e}{Variable\+\_\+\+ID}} $>$}]{excluded\+\_\+floor\+\_\+vars = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{gmp__compat_8h_a1e8c092646181d922b1412a0b41dcfde}{std\+::set}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a3d38f72333aae2d1dd9b772059c2ee3e}{Variable\+\_\+\+ID}}$>$()} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

@breif find floor definition for wildcard variable v e.\+g. m-\/c $<$= 4v $<$= m, (c is constant and 0 $<$= c $<$ 4). this translates to v = floor(m, 4) and return 4v$<$=m in this case. All wildcards in such inequality are also floor defined. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:

\begin{center}

\end{center}
\end{figure}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{find\_simplest\_assignment()}{find\_simplest\_assignment()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_e_q___handle}{E\+Q\+\_\+\+Handle}}, int $>$ omega\+::find\+\_\+simplest\+\_\+assignment (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{gen-psqr_8c_a2c212835823e3c54a8ab6d95c652660e}{const}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a3d38f72333aae2d1dd9b772059c2ee3e}{Variable\+\_\+\+ID}}}]{v,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{gen-psqr_8c_a2c212835823e3c54a8ab6d95c652660e}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_c_g__output_repr}{C\+G\+\_\+output\+Repr}} $\ast$, int $>$ $>$ \&}]{assigned\+\_\+on\+\_\+the\+\_\+fly = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:vector$<$std\+:\+:pair$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_c_g__output_repr}{C\+G\+\_\+output\+Repr}}~$\ast$,~int$>$~$>$()},  }\item[{bool $\ast$}]{has\+\_\+global\+\_\+inspector = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{_profiler_8hpp_a070d2ce7b6bb7e5c05602aa8c308d0c4}{N\+U\+LL}}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Find the simplest(cheapest by cost function) assignment of variable v This handles floor definition wildcards in equality, the second in returned pair is the cost.

\index{omega@{omega}!LinearHull@{LinearHull}}
\index{LinearHull@{LinearHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{LinearHull()}{LinearHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Linear\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{R }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Linear Hull using linear combination. 

Linear combination is the convex combination without constraints on a\+\_\+i\+: \[x \in Linear(S) \iff \exists y_i \in S, \exists a_i \in R: x = \sum_i a_iy_i\] This will first call approximate on R to eliminate any wildcards and strides \begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceomega_a1c21a38b01729e780825f69d73ef7fb9}{Convex\+Hull}}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceomega_ad69edb2e5481584853a04b18984fcad3}\label{namespaceomega_ad69edb2e5481584853a04b18984fcad3}} 
\index{omega@{omega}!RectHull@{RectHull}}
\index{RectHull@{RectHull}!omega@{omega}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{RectHull()}{RectHull()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} omega\+::\+Rect\+Hull (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{pres__gen_8h_a6d4b5128eccebf63d2b2f175182c0489}{N\+O\+T\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+ST}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classomega_1_1_relation}{Relation}} \&}]{Rel }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculate the Rect Hull. 

Rect\+Hull includes readily-\/available constraints from relation that can be part of hull, plus rectangular bounds calculated from input/output/set variables\textquotesingle{} range.

This uses gist and value range to calculate a quick rectangular hull. It intends to replace all hull calculations (Quick\+Hull, Better\+Hull, Fast\+Tight\+Hull) beyond the method of Convex\+Hull (dual representations). In the future, it will support \mbox{\hyperlink{linalg_8h_ac39d9cef6a5e030ba8d9e11121054268}{max(...)}}-\/like upper bound. So Rect\+Hull complements Convex\+Hull in two ways\+: first for relations that Convex\+Hull gets too complicated, second for relations where different conjuncts have different symbolic upper bounds. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:
\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{namespaceomega_ad69edb2e5481584853a04b18984fcad3_icgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}

replicate the floor definition(possibly cascaded to new relation) parameter f\+\_\+root is inside f\+\_\+exists, not the other way around. return replicated variable in new relation, with all cascaded floor definitions using wildcards defined in the same way as in the original relation.
